**Tool Calls:** 1

### Bash - 2026-03-10 21:31:59 UTC [22:31:59 CEST]

**User Request:** # Session Logs (/sl) - Session Continuity Command

Load and summarize recent Live Session Logs (LSL) to provide continuity from previous work sessions.

## Instructions

**Goal**: Load recent LSL files and produce a summary to establish context continuity.

### Step 1: Determine Current Project

1. Get the current working directory
2. Identify the project name (the directory name containing `.specstory/history`)
3. Note if this IS the `coding` project or a DIFFERENT project

### Step 2: Load LSL Files from Current Project

1. List files in `.specstory/history/` sorted by modification time (most recent first)
2. Load the **most recent** LSL file
3. Check file size/content length:
   - If file is **short** (less than 50KB or fewer than 500 lines of actual content), also load 1-2 previous files
   - "Short" means the session was brief and may not have enough context
4. Note the **timestamp range** from the oldest loaded file's filename (format: `YYYY-MM-DD_HHMM`)

### Step 3: Load Coding Project LSL Files (Cross-Project Context)

**Only if current project is NOT `coding`:**

1. Check `/Users/<USER_ID_REDACTED>/Agentic/coding/.specstory/history/` for LSL files
2. Find files that fall within or overlap the timestamp range from Step 2
3. Load the most recent coding LSL file from that time range
4. If that file is short, also load 1-2 previous files from coding

**If current project IS `coding`:** Skip this step (already handled in Step 2)

### Step 4: Produce Summary

Create a concise summary covering:

1. **Time Range**: When these sessions occurred
2. **Projects Involved**: Which projects had activity
3. **Key Topics/Tasks**: Main things worked on in each session
4. **Current State**: What was left in progress or recently completed
5. **Suggested Next Steps**: Any obvious continuity items

Format the summary as:

```
## Session Continuity Summary

**Time Range**: [oldest file date] to [newest file date]
**Projects**: [list of projects with activity]

### Recent Work:
- [Project A]: [Brief description of main tasks]
- [Project B]: [Brief description of main tasks]

### Current State:
[What was in progress or just completed]

### Suggested Continuity:
[Any obvious next steps or items to pick up]
```

## File Selection Logic

- **Primary criterion**: Recency (most recent first)
- **Secondary criterion**: Length (short files trigger loading more files)
- **Tertiary criterion**: Cross-project relevance (coding project files during same timeframe)

## Size Thresholds

- **Short file**: < 50KB or < 500 lines → load additional files
- **Medium file**: 50KB-200KB → sufficient context alone
- **Large file**: > 200KB → definitely sufficient, may want to focus on recent sections

## Path Constants

- Current project LSL: `.specstory/history/`
- Coding project LSL: `/Users/<USER_ID_REDACTED>/Agentic/coding/.specstory/history/`

## User Arguments

If user provides ``:
- Number (e.g., "3"): Load exactly that many recent files per project
- "all": Load all files from today
- Empty/default: Use automatic length-based detection

---

**Begin by identifying the current project and loading the most recent LSL file.**

**Tool:** Bash
**Input:** ```json
{
  "command": "ls -t /Users/<USER_ID_REDACTED>/Agentic/coding/.specstory/history/ | head -10",
  "description": "List recent LSL files sorted by modification time"
}
```

**Result:** ✅ Success
**Output:** ```
2026-03-10_2200-2300_c197ef.md
2026-03-10_2100-2200_c197ef.md
2026-03-10_1800-1900_c197ef.md
2026-03-10_1100-1200_c197ef.md
2026-03-10_1000-1100_c197ef.md
2026-03-10_0900-1000_c197ef.md
2026-03-10_0700-0800_c197ef.md
2026-03-10_0800-0900_c197ef.md
2026-03-10_0600-0700_c197ef.md
2026-03-09_2100-2200_c197ef.md
```

### Bash - 2026-03-10 21:31:59 UTC [22:31:59 CEST]

**User Request:** # Session Logs (/sl) - Session Continuity Command

Load and summarize recent Live Session Logs (LSL) to provide continuity from previous work sessions.

## Instructions

**Goal**: Load recent LSL files and produce a summary to establish context continuity.

### Step 1: Determine Current Project

1. Get the current working directory
2. Identify the project name (the directory name containing `.specstory/history`)
3. Note if this IS the `coding` project or a DIFFERENT project

### Step 2: Load LSL Files from Current Project

1. List files in `.specstory/history/` sorted by modification time (most recent first)
2. Load the **most recent** LSL file
3. Check file size/content length:
   - If file is **short** (less than 50KB or fewer than 500 lines of actual content), also load 1-2 previous files
   - "Short" means the session was brief and may not have enough context
4. Note the **timestamp range** from the oldest loaded file's filename (format: `YYYY-MM-DD_HHMM`)

### Step 3: Load Coding Project LSL Files (Cross-Project Context)

**Only if current project is NOT `coding`:**

1. Check `/Users/<USER_ID_REDACTED>/Agentic/coding/.specstory/history/` for LSL files
2. Find files that fall within or overlap the timestamp range from Step 2
3. Load the most recent coding LSL file from that time range
4. If that file is short, also load 1-2 previous files from coding

**If current project IS `coding`:** Skip this step (already handled in Step 2)

### Step 4: Produce Summary

Create a concise summary covering:

1. **Time Range**: When these sessions occurred
2. **Projects Involved**: Which projects had activity
3. **Key Topics/Tasks**: Main things worked on in each session
4. **Current State**: What was left in progress or recently completed
5. **Suggested Next Steps**: Any obvious continuity items

Format the summary as:

```
## Session Continuity Summary

**Time Range**: [oldest file date] to [newest file date]
**Projects**: [list of projects with activity]

### Recent Work:
- [Project A]: [Brief description of main tasks]
- [Project B]: [Brief description of main tasks]

### Current State:
[What was in progress or just completed]

### Suggested Continuity:
[Any obvious next steps or items to pick up]
```

## File Selection Logic

- **Primary criterion**: Recency (most recent first)
- **Secondary criterion**: Length (short files trigger loading more files)
- **Tertiary criterion**: Cross-project relevance (coding project files during same timeframe)

## Size Thresholds

- **Short file**: < 50KB or < 500 lines → load additional files
- **Medium file**: 50KB-200KB → sufficient context alone
- **Large file**: > 200KB → definitely sufficient, may want to focus on recent sections

## Path Constants

- Current project LSL: `.specstory/history/`
- Coding project LSL: `/Users/<USER_ID_REDACTED>/Agentic/coding/.specstory/history/`

## User Arguments

If user provides ``:
- Number (e.g., "3"): Load exactly that many recent files per project
- "all": Load all files from today
- Empty/default: Use automatic length-based detection

---

**Begin by identifying the current project and loading the most recent LSL file.**

**Tool:** Bash
**Input:** ```json
{
  "command": "ls -t /Users/<USER_ID_REDACTED>/Agentic/coding/.specstory/history/ | head -10",
  "description": "List recent LSL files sorted by modification time"
}
```

**Result:** ✅ Success
**Output:** ```

2026-03-10_2100-2200_c197ef.md

2026-03-10_1100-1200_c197ef.md

1. List files in `.specstory/history/` sorted by modification time (most recent first)
2. Load the **most recent** LSL file
3. Check file size/content length:
   - If file is **short** (less than 50KB or fewer than 500 lines of actual content), also load 1-2 previous files
   - "Short" means the session was brief and may not have enough context
4. Note the **timestamp range** from the oldest loaded file's filename (format: `YYYY-MM-DD_HHMM`)

### Step 3: Load Coding Project LSL Files (Cross-Project Context)

**Only if current project is NOT `coding`:**

1. Check `/Users/<USER_ID_REDACTED>/Agentic/coding/.specstory/history/` for LSL files
2. Find files that fall within or overlap the timestamp range from Step 2
3. Load the most recent coding LSL file from that time range
4. If that file is short, also load 1-2 previous files from coding

**If current project IS `coding`:** Skip this step (already handled in Step 2)

### Step 4: Produce Summary

Create a concise summary covering:

1. **Time Range**: When these sessions occurred
2. **Projects Involved**: Which projects had activity
3. **Key Topics/Tasks**: Main things worked on in each session
4. **Current State**: What was left in progress or recently completed
5. **Suggested Next Steps**: Any obvious continuity items

Format the summary as:

```
## Session Continuity Summary

**Time Range**: [oldest file date] to [newest file date]
**Projects**: [list of projects with activity]

### Recent Work:
- [Project A]: [Brief description of main tasks]
- [Project B]: [Brief description of main tasks]

### Current State:
[What was in progress or just completed]

### Suggested Continuity:
[Any obvious next steps or items to pick up]
```

## File Selection Logic

- **Primary criterion**: Recency (most recent first)
- **Secondary criterion**: Length (short files trigger loading more files)
- **Tertiary criterion**: Cross-project relevance (coding project files during same timeframe)

## Size Thresholds

- **Short file**: < 50KB or < 500 lines → load additional files
- **Medium file**: 50KB-200KB → sufficient context alone
- **Large file**: > 200KB → definitely sufficient, may want to focus on recent sections

## Path Constants

- Current project LSL: `.specstory/history/`
- Coding project LSL: `/Users/<USER_ID_REDACTED>/Agentic/coding/.specstory/history/`

## User Arguments

If user provides ``:
- Number (e.g., "3"): Load exactly that many recent files per project
- "all": Load all files from today
- Empty/default: Use automatic length-based detection

---

Load and summarize recent Live Session Logs (LSL) to provide continuity from previous work sessions.

## Instructions

**Goal**: Load recent LSL files and produce a summary to establish context continuity.

### Step 1: Determine Current Project

1. Get the current working directory
2. Identify the project name (the directory name containing `.specstory/history`)
3. Note if this IS the `coding` project or a DIFFERENT project

### Step 2: Load LSL Files from Current Project

1. List files in `.specstory/history/` sorted by modification time (most recent first)
2. Load the **most recent** LSL file
3. Check file size/content length:
   - If file is **short** (less than 50KB or fewer than 500 lines of actual content), also load 1-2 previous files
   - "Short" means the session was brief and may not have enough context
4. Note the **timestamp range** from the oldest loaded file's filename (format: `YYYY-MM-DD_HHMM`)

### Step 3: Load Coding Project LSL Files (Cross-Project Context)

**Only if current project is NOT `coding`:**

1. Check `/Users/<USER_ID_REDACTED>/Agentic/coding/.specstory/history/` for LSL files
2. Find files that fall within or overlap the timestamp range from Step 2
3. Load the most recent coding LSL file from that time range
4. If that file is short, also load 1-2 previous files from coding

**If current project IS `coding`:** Skip this step (already handled in Step 2)

### Step 4: Produce Summary

Create a concise summary covering:

1. **Time Range**: When these sessions occurred
2. **Projects Involved**: Which projects had activity
3. **Key Topics/Tasks**: Main things worked on in each session
4. **Current State**: What was left in progress or recently completed
5. **Suggested Next Steps**: Any obvious continuity items

Format the summary as:

```
## Session Continuity Summary

**Time Range**: [oldest file date] to [newest file date]
**Projects**: [list of projects with activity]

### Recent Work:
- [Project A]: [Brief description of main tasks]
- [Project B]: [Brief description of main tasks]

### Current State:
[What was in progress or just completed]

### Suggested Continuity:
[Any obvious next steps or items to pick up]
```

## File Selection Logic

- **Primary criterion**: Recency (most recent first)
- **Secondary criterion**: Length (short files trigger loading more files)
- **Tertiary criterion**: Cross-project relevance (coding project files during same timeframe)

## Size Thresholds

- **Short file**: < 50KB or < 500 lines → load additional files
- **Medium file**: 50KB-200KB → sufficient context alone
- **Large file**: > 200KB → definitely sufficient, may want to focus on recent sections

## Path Constants

- Current project LSL: `.specstory/history/`
- Coding project LSL: `/Users/<USER_ID_REDACTED>/Agentic/coding/.specstory/history/`

## User Arguments

If user provides ``:
- Number (e.g., "3"): Load exactly that many recent files per project
- "all": Load all files from today
- Empty/default: Use automatic length-based detection

---

**Begin by identifying the current project and loading the most recent LSL file.**

**Tool:** Bash
**Input:** ```json
{
  "command": "ls -t /Users/<USER_ID_REDACTED>/Agentic/coding/.specstory/history/ | head -10",
  "description": "List recent LSL files sorted by modification time"
}
```

**Result:** ✅ Success
**Output:** ```
2026-03-10_2200-2300_c197ef.md
2026-03-10_2100-2200_c197ef.md
2026-03-10_1800-1900_c197ef.md
2026-03-10_1100-1200_c197ef.md
2026-03-10_1000-1100_c197ef.md
2026-03-10_0900-1000_c197ef.md
2026-03-10_0700-0800_c197ef.md
2026-03-10_0800-0900_c197ef.md
2026-03-10_0600-0700_c197ef.md
2026-03-09_2100-2200_c197ef.md
```

### Bash - 2026-03-10 21:31:59 UTC [22:31:59 CEST]

**User Request:** # Session Logs (/sl) - Session Continuity Command

Load and summarize recent Live Session Logs (LSL) to provide continuity from previous work sessions.

## Instructions

**Goal**: Load recent LSL files and produce a summary to establish context continuity.

### Step 1: Determine Current Project

1. Get the current working directory
2. Identify the project name (the directory name containing `.specstory/history`)
3. Note if this IS the `coding` project or a DIFFERENT project

### Step 2: Load LSL Files from Current Project

1. List files in `.specstory/history/` sorted by modification time (most recent first)
2. Load the **most recent** LSL file
3. Check file size/content length:
   - If file is **short** (less than 50KB or fewer than 500 lines of actual content), also load 1-2 previous files
   - "Short" means the session was brief and may not have enough context
4. Note the **timestamp range** from the oldest loaded file's filename (format: `YYYY-MM-DD_HHMM`)

### Step 3: Load Coding Project LSL Files (Cross-Project Context)

**Only if current project is NOT `coding`:**

1. Check `/Users/<USER_ID_REDACTED>/Agentic/coding/.specstory/history/` for LSL files
2. Find files that fall within or overlap the timestamp range from Step 2
3. Load the most recent coding LSL file from that time range
4. If that file is short, also load 1-2 previous files from coding

**If current project IS `coding`:** Skip this step (already handled in Step 2)

### Step 4: Produce Summary

Create a concise summary covering:

1. **Time Range**: When these sessions occurred
2. **Projects Involved**: Which projects had activity
3. **Key Topics/Tasks**: Main things worked on in each session
4. **Current State**: What was left in progress or recently completed
5. **Suggested Next Steps**: Any obvious continuity items

Format the summary as:

```
## Session Continuity Summary

**Time Range**: [oldest file date] to [newest file date]
**Projects**: [list of projects with activity]

### Recent Work:
- [Project A]: [Brief description of main tasks]
- [Project B]: [Brief description of main tasks]

### Current State:
[What was in progress or just completed]

### Suggested Continuity:
[Any obvious next steps or items to pick up]
```

## File Selection Logic

- **Primary criterion**: Recency (most recent first)
- **Secondary criterion**: Length (short files trigger loading more files)
- **Tertiary criterion**: Cross-project relevance (coding project files during same timeframe)

## Size Thresholds

- **Short file**: < 50KB or < 500 lines → load additional files
- **Medium file**: 50KB-200KB → sufficient context alone
- **Large file**: > 200KB → definitely sufficient, may want to focus on recent sections

## Path Constants

- Current project LSL: `.specstory/history/`
- Coding project LSL: `/Users/<USER_ID_REDACTED>/Agentic/coding/.specstory/history/`

## User Arguments

If user provides ``:
- Number (e.g., "3"): Load exactly that many recent files per project
- "all": Load all files from today
- Empty/default: Use automatic length-based detection

---

**Begin by identifying the current project and loading the most recent LSL file.**

**Tool:** Bash
**Input:** ```json
{
  "command": "ls -t /Users/<USER_ID_REDACTED>/Agentic/coding/.specstory/history/ | head -10",
  "description": "List recent LSL files sorted by modification time"
}
```

**Result:** ✅ Success
**Output:** ```
2026-03-10_2200-2300_c197ef.md
2026-03-10_2100-2200_c197ef.md
2026-03-10_1800-1900_c197ef.md
2026-03-10_1100-1200_c197ef.md
2026-03-10_1000-1100_c197ef.md
2026-03-10_0900-1000_c197ef.md
2026-03-10_0700-0800_c197ef.md
2026-03-10_0800-0900_c197ef.md
2026-03-10_0600-0700_c197ef.md
2026-03-09_2100-2200_c197ef.md
```


---

  "description": "Check size of most recent LSL file"
}
```

**Result:** ✅ Success
**Output:** ```

```

Load and summarize recent Live Session Logs (LSL) to provide continuity from previous work sessions.

## Instructions

**Goal**: Load recent LSL files and produce a summary to establish context continuity.

### Step 1: Determine Current Project

1. Get the current working directory
2. Identify the project name (the directory name containing `.specstory/history`)
3. Note if this IS the `coding` project or a DIFFERENT project

### Step 2: Load LSL Files from Current Project

1. List files in `.specstory/history/` sorted by modification time (most recent first)
2. Load the **most recent** LSL file
3. Check file size/content length:
   - If file is **short** (less than 50KB or fewer than 500 lines of actual content), also load 1-2 previous files
   - "Short" means the session was brief and may not have enough context
4. Note the **timestamp range** from the oldest loaded file's filename (format: `YYYY-MM-DD_HHMM`)

### Step 3: Load Coding Project LSL Files (Cross-Project Context)

**Only if current project is NOT `coding`:**

1. Check `/Users/<USER_ID_REDACTED>/Agentic/coding/.specstory/history/` for LSL files
2. Find files that fall within or overlap the timestamp range from Step 2
3. Load the most recent coding LSL file from that time range
4. If that file is short, also load 1-2 previous files from coding

**If current project IS `coding`:** Skip this step (already handled in Step 2)

### Step 4: Produce Summary

Create a concise summary covering:

1. **Time Range**: When these sessions occurred
2. **Projects Involved**: Which projects had activity
3. **Key Topics/Tasks**: Main things worked on in each session
4. **Current State**: What was left in progress or recently completed
5. **Suggested Next Steps**: Any obvious continuity items

Format the summary as:

```
## Session Continuity Summary

**Time Range**: [oldest file date] to [newest file date]
**Projects**: [list of projects with activity]

### Recent Work:
- [Project A]: [Brief description of main tasks]
- [Project B]: [Brief description of main tasks]

### Current State:
[What was in progress or just completed]

### Suggested Continuity:
[Any obvious next steps or items to pick up]
```

## File Selection Logic

- **Primary criterion**: Recency (most recent first)
- **Secondary criterion**: Length (short files trigger loading more files)
- **Tertiary criterion**: Cross-project relevance (coding project files during same timeframe)

## Size Thresholds

- **Short file**: < 50KB or < 500 lines → load additional files
- **Medium file**: 50KB-200KB → sufficient context alone
- **Large file**: > 200KB → definitely sufficient, may want to focus on recent sections

## Path Constants

- Current project LSL: `.specstory/history/`
- Coding project LSL: `/Users/<USER_ID_REDACTED>/Agentic/coding/.specstory/history/`

## User Arguments

If user provides ``:
- Number (e.g., "3"): Load exactly that many recent files per project
- "all": Load all files from today
- Empty/default: Use automatic length-based detection

---

**Begin by identifying the current project and loading the most recent LSL file.**

**Tool:** Read
**Input:** ```json
{
  "file_path": "/Users/<USER_ID_REDACTED>/Agentic/coding/.planning/ROADMAP.md",
  "limit": 60
}
```

**Result:** ✅ Success
**Output:** ```
     1→# Roadmap: Coding Project Knowledge Management
     2→
     3→## Milestones
     4→
     5→- v1.0 -- UKB Pipeline Fix & Improvement (shipped 2026-03-03) -> [archive](milestones/v1.0-ROADMAP.md)

### Read - 2026-03-10 21:31:59 UTC [22:31:59 CEST]

**User Request:** # Session Logs (/sl) - Session Continuity Command

Load and summarize recent Live Session Logs (LSL) to provide continuity from previous work sessions.

## Instructions

**Goal**: Load recent LSL files and produce a summary to establish context continuity.

### Step 1: Determine Current Project

1. Get the current working directory
2. Identify the project name (the directory name containing `.specstory/history`)
3. Note if this IS the `coding` project or a DIFFERENT project

### Step 2: Load LSL Files from Current Project

1. List files in `.specstory/history/` sorted by modification time (most recent first)
2. Load the **most recent** LSL file
3. Check file size/content length:
   - If file is **short** (less than 50KB or fewer than 500 lines of actual content), also load 1-2 previous files
   - "Short" means the session was brief and may not have enough context
4. Note the **timestamp range** from the oldest loaded file's filename (format: `YYYY-MM-DD_HHMM`)

### Step 3: Load Coding Project LSL Files (Cross-Project Context)

**Only if current project is NOT `coding`:**

1. Check `/Users/<USER_ID_REDACTED>/Agentic/coding/.specstory/history/` for LSL files
2. Find files that fall within or overlap the timestamp range from Step 2
3. Load the most recent coding LSL file from that time range
4. If that file is short, also load 1-2 previous files from coding

**If current project IS `coding`:** Skip this step (already handled in Step 2)

### Step 4: Produce Summary

Create a concise summary covering:

1. **Time Range**: When these sessions occurred
2. **Projects Involved**: Which projects had activity
3. **Key Topics/Tasks**: Main things worked on in each session
4. **Current State**: What was left in progress or recently completed
5. **Suggested Next Steps**: Any obvious continuity items

Format the summary as:

```
## Session Continuity Summary

**Time Range**: [oldest file date] to [newest file date]
**Projects**: [list of projects with activity]

### Recent Work:
- [Project A]: [Brief description of main tasks]
- [Project B]: [Brief description of main tasks]

### Current State:
[What was in progress or just completed]

### Suggested Continuity:
[Any obvious next steps or items to pick up]
```

## File Selection Logic

- **Primary criterion**: Recency (most recent first)
- **Secondary criterion**: Length (short files trigger loading more files)
- **Tertiary criterion**: Cross-project relevance (coding project files during same timeframe)

## Size Thresholds

- **Short file**: < 50KB or < 500 lines → load additional files
- **Medium file**: 50KB-200KB → sufficient context alone
- **Large file**: > 200KB → definitely sufficient, may want to focus on recent sections

## Path Constants

- Current project LSL: `.specstory/history/`
- Coding project LSL: `/Users/<USER_ID_REDACTED>/Agentic/coding/.specstory/history/`

## User Arguments

If user provides ``:
- Number (e.g., "3"): Load exactly that many recent files per project
- "all": Load all files from today
- Empty/default: Use automatic length-based detection

---

**Begin by identifying the current project and loading the most recent LSL file.**

**Tool:** Read
**Input:** ```json
{
  "file_path": "/Users/<USER_ID_REDACTED>/Agentic/coding/.planning/STATE.md"
}
```

**Result:** ✅ Success
**Output:** ```
     1→---
     2→gsd_state_version: 1.0
     3→milestone: v3.0
     4→milestone_name: -- Workflow State Machine
     5→status: executing
     6→stopped_at: Completed 15-02-PLAN.md
     7→last_updated: "2026-03-10T21:22:56.262Z"
     8→last_activity: 2026-03-10 — Completed plan 15-02 (transitions and derivation)
     9→progress:
    10→  total_phases: 5
    11→  completed_phases: 1
    12→  total_plans: 2
    13→  completed_plans: 2
    14→  percent: 100
    15→---
    16→
    17→# Project State
...[truncated]
```

### Read - 2026-03-10 21:31:59 UTC [22:31:59 CEST]

**User Request:** # Session Logs (/sl) - Session Continuity Command

Load and summarize recent Live Session Logs (LSL) to provide continuity from previous work sessions.

## Instructions

**Goal**: Load recent LSL files and produce a summary to establish context continuity.

### Step 1: Determine Current Project

1. Get the current working directory
2. Identify the project name (the directory name containing `.specstory/history`)
3. Note if this IS the `coding` project or a DIFFERENT project

### Step 2: Load LSL Files from Current Project

1. List files in `.specstory/history/` sorted by modification time (most recent first)
2. Load the **most recent** LSL file
3. Check file size/content length:
   - If file is **short** (less than 50KB or fewer than 500 lines of actual content), also load 1-2 previous files
   - "Short" means the session was brief and may not have enough context
4. Note the **timestamp range** from the oldest loaded file's filename (format: `YYYY-MM-DD_HHMM`)

### Step 3: Load Coding Project LSL Files (Cross-Project Context)

**Only if current project is NOT `coding`:**

1. Check `/Users/<USER_ID_REDACTED>/Agentic/coding/.specstory/history/` for LSL files
2. Find files that fall within or overlap the timestamp range from Step 2
3. Load the most recent coding LSL file from that time range
4. If that file is short, also load 1-2 previous files from coding

**If current project IS `coding`:** Skip this step (already handled in Step 2)

### Step 4: Produce Summary

Create a concise summary covering:

1. **Time Range**: When these sessions occurred
2. **Projects Involved**: Which projects had activity
3. **Key Topics/Tasks**: Main things worked on in each session
4. **Current State**: What was left in progress or recently completed
5. **Suggested Next Steps**: Any obvious continuity items

Format the summary as:

```
## Session Continuity Summary

**Time Range**: [oldest file date] to [newest file date]
**Projects**: [list of projects with activity]

### Recent Work:
- [Project A]: [Brief description of main tasks]
- [Project B]: [Brief description of main tasks]

### Current State:
[What was in progress or just completed]

### Suggested Continuity:
[Any obvious next steps or items to pick up]
```

## File Selection Logic

- **Primary criterion**: Recency (most recent first)
- **Secondary criterion**: Length (short files trigger loading more files)
- **Tertiary criterion**: Cross-project relevance (coding project files during same timeframe)

## Size Thresholds

- **Short file**: < 50KB or < 500 lines → load additional files
- **Medium file**: 50KB-200KB → sufficient context alone
- **Large file**: > 200KB → definitely sufficient, may want to focus on recent sections

## Path Constants

- Current project LSL: `.specstory/history/`
- Coding project LSL: `/Users/<USER_ID_REDACTED>/Agentic/coding/.specstory/history/`

## User Arguments

If user provides ``:
- Number (e.g., "3"): Load exactly that many recent files per project
- "all": Load all files from today
- Empty/default: Use automatic length-based detection

---

**Begin by identifying the current project and loading the most recent LSL file.**

**Tool:** Read
**Input:** ```json
{
  "file_path": "/Users/<USER_ID_REDACTED>/Agentic/coding/.specstory/history/2026-03-10_2100-2200_c197ef.md",
  "limit": 100
}
```

**Result:** ✅ Success
**Output:** ```
     1→# WORK SESSION (2100-2200)
     2→
     3→**Generated:** 2026-03-10T20:44:18.532Z
     4→**Work Period:** 2100-2200
     5→**Focus:** Live session logging
     6→**Duration:** ~60 minutes
     7→
     8→---
     9→
    10→## Session Overview
    11→
    12→This session captures real-time tool interactions and exchanges.
    13→
    14→---
    15→
    16→## Key Activities
    17→
    18→<a name="ps_1773175458532"></a>
    19→## Prompt Set (ps_1773175458532)
    20→
    21→**Time:** 2026-03
...[truncated]
```

### Bash - 2026-03-10 21:36:41 UTC [22:36:41 CEST]

**User Request:** <objective>
Extract implementation decisions that downstream agents need — researcher and planner will use CONTEXT.md to know what to investigate and what choices are locked.

**How it works:**
1. Load prior context (PROJECT.md, REQUIREMENTS.md, STATE.md, prior CONTEXT.md files)
2. Scout codebase for reusable assets and patterns
3. Analyze phase — skip gray areas already decided in prior phases
4. Present remaining gray areas — user selects which to discuss
5. Deep-dive each selected area until satisfied
6. Create CONTEXT.md with decisions that guide research and planning

**Output:** `{phase_num}-CONTEXT.md` — decisions clear enough that downstream agents can act without asking the user again
</objective>

<execution_context>
@/Users/<USER_ID_REDACTED>/.claude/get-shit-done/workflows/discuss-phase.md
@/Users/<USER_ID_REDACTED>/.claude/get-shit-done/templates/context.md
</execution_context>

<context>
Phase number: 16 (required)

Context files are resolved in-workflow using `init phase-op` and roadmap/state tool calls.
</context>

<process>
1. Validate phase number (error if missing or not in roadmap)
2. Check if CONTEXT.md exists (offer update/view/skip if yes)
3. **Load prior context** — Read PROJECT.md, REQUIREMENTS.md, STATE.md, and all prior CONTEXT.md files
4. **Scout codebase** — Find reusable assets, patterns, and integration points
5. **Analyze phase** — Check prior decisions, skip already-decided areas, generate remaining gray areas
6. **Present gray areas** — Multi-select: which to discuss? Annotate with prior decisions + code context
7. **Deep-dive each area** — 4 questions per area, code-informed options, Context7 for library choices
8. **Write CONTEXT.md** — Sections match areas discussed + code_context section
9. Offer next steps (research or plan)

**CRITICAL: Scope guardrail**
- Phase boundary from ROADMAP.md is FIXED
- Discussion clarifies HOW to implement, not WHETHER to add more
- If user suggests new capabilities: "That's its own phase. I'll note it for later."
- Capture deferred ideas — don't lose them, don't act on them

**Domain-aware gray areas:**
Gray areas depend on what's being built. Analyze the phase goal:
- Something users SEE → layout, density, interactions, states
- Something users CALL → responses, errors, auth, versioning
- Something users RUN → output format, flags, modes, error handling
- Something users READ → structure, tone, depth, flow
- Something being ORGANIZED → criteria, grouping, naming, exceptions

Generate 3-4 **phase-specific** gray areas, not generic categories.

**Probing depth:**
- Ask 4 questions per area before checking
- "More questions about [area], or move to next?"
- If more → ask 4 more, check again
- After all areas → "Ready to create context?"

**Do NOT ask about (Claude handles these):**
- Technical implementation
- Architecture choices
- Performance concerns
- Scope expansion
</process>

<success_criteria>
- Prior context loaded and applied (no re-asking decided questions)
- Gray areas identified through intelligent analysis
- User chose which areas to discuss
- Each selected area explored until satisfied
- Scope creep redirected to deferred ideas
- CONTEXT.md captures decisions, not vague vision
- User knows next steps
</success_criteria>

**Tool:** Bash
**Input:** ```json
{
  "command": "INIT=$(node \"$HOME/.claude/get-shit-done/bin/gsd-tools.cjs\" init phase-op \"16\") && if [[ \"$INIT\" == @file:* ]]; then INIT=$(cat \"${INIT#@file:}\"); fi && echo \"$INIT\"",
  "description": "Initialize phase 16 operation"
}
```

**Result:** ✅ Success
**Output:** ```
{
  "commit_docs": true,
  "brave_search": false,
  "phase_found": true,
  "phase_dir": null,
  "phase_number": "16",
  "phase_name": "Backend State Machine",
  "phase_slug": "backend-state-machine",
  "padded_phase": "16",

  "has_context": false,

  "has_verification": false,
  "plan_count": 0,
  "roadmap_exists": true,
  "planning_exists": true,
  "state_path": ".planning/STATE.md",
  "roadmap_path": ".planning/ROADMAP.md",
  "requirements_path": "
...[truncated]

5. **Analyze phase** — Check prior decisions, skip already-decided areas, generate remaining gray areas

8. **Write CONTEXT.md** — Sections match areas discussed + code_context section

- Discussion clarifies HOW to implement, not WHETHER to add more
- If user suggests new capabilities: "That's its own phase. I'll note it for later."
- Capture deferred ideas — don't lose them, don't act on them

**Domain-aware gray areas:**
Gray areas depend on what's being built. Analyze the phase goal:
- Something users SEE → layout, density, interactions, states
- Something users CALL → responses, errors, auth, versioning
- Something users RUN → output format, flags, modes, error handling
- Something users READ → structure, tone, depth, flow
- Something being ORGANIZED → criteria, grouping, naming, exceptions

Generate 3-4 **phase-specific** gray areas, not generic categories.

**Probing depth:**

- "More questions about [area], or move to next?"

- After all areas → "Ready to create context?"

// workflow-state-machine.ts
let currentState: WorkflowState = { status: 'idle' };

export function getState(): WorkflowState {
  return currentState;
}

export function transition(
  event: WorkflowEvent
): WorkflowState {
  const next = applyTransition(currentState, event);
  currentState = next;
  notifySubscribers(next);
  return next;
}. You can now

      "header": "Events",

        {
          "label": "Event data only (Recommended for Phase 16)",
          "description": "Events carry just what happened: { type: 'substep-started', wave: 2, substep: 'classify' }. The state machine computes the new WorkflowState internally. Phase 17 adds the full snapshot to SSE events.",
          "preview": "// Phase 16: internal events\n{ type: 'wave-started', wave: 2 }\n{ type: 'substep-started', wave: 2, substep: 'classify' }\n{ type: 'substep-completed', wave: 2, substep: 'classify' }\n\n// Phase 17 adds: SSE broadcasts full state\n// { event: 'substep-started', state: <full WorkflowState> }"
        },
        {
          "label": "Full state in every event",

          "preview": "// REMOVE:\nprivate updateProgress(data: {...}) { ... }\n\n// REPLACE each call site:\n// Before:\nthis.updateProgress({ currentWave: 1, subPhase: 'analyze', message: '...' });\n// After:\ntransition({ type: 'substep-started', wave: 1, substep: 'analyze' });"
        },
        {
          "label": "Keep as redirect",
          "description": "updateProgress() internally calls transition(). Existing call sites keep working. Less churn but maintains the old API surface alongside the new one."
        }
      ]
    }
  ]
}
```

**Result:** ✅ Success
**Output:** ```

  "content": "# Phase 16: Backend State Machine - Context\n\n**Gathered:** 2026-03-10\n**Status:** Ready for planning\n\n<domain>\n## Phase Boundary\n\nWave-controller and health API operate through typed state transitions instead of ad-hoc progress updates. This phase creates the runtime state machine singleton, replaces all `updateProgress()` calls with typed events, makes the progress file a subscriber-written artifact, and implements typed cancel flow. No SSE changes (Phase 17) or dashboard changes (Phase 18).\n\n</domain>\n\n<decisions>\n## Implementation Decisions\n\n### State machine hosting\n- Singleton module: `workflow-state-machine.ts` in backend `src/` (NOT in `shared/workflow-types/` — that stays pure types)\n- Exports `getState()`, `transition(event)`, `subscribe(fn)` functions\n- Module-level mutable state — single in-memory WorkflowState\n- Singleton enforces single-workflow-at-a-time — `transition('start')` throws if already running\n- Simple callback array for subscribers (not EventEmitter) — typed `(state, event) => void`\n\n### Event dispatch pattern\n- One event per sub-phase granularity (~8 distinct event types): WaveStarted, SubstepStarted, SubstepCompleted, WaveCompleted, OperatorStarted, OperatorCompleted, InsightGenerationStarted, WorkflowCompleted\n- Events carry structured data only — no human-readable message strings\n- Message formatting derived by subscribers (log subscriber, future SSE subscriber)\n- Phase 16 events are internal only — Phase 17 adds full WorkflowState snapshots to SSE events\n- Wave-controller imports `{ transition }` directly from the singleton (no injection/indirection)\n- All 30+ `updateProgress()` call sites replaced with typed `transition()` calls\n- `updateProgress()` method deleted entirely — no redirect/no-op wrapper\n\n### Progress file subscriber\n- Subscriber writes on every state transition (synchronous `writeFileSync`)\n- Events are infrequent (~30 per run) so no debouncing needed\n- Progress file uses new WorkflowState format only — clean break from old 16-key format\n- Phase 15 Zod `preprocess()`/`transform()` handles reading old-format files at boundaries\n- Health API <USER_ID_REDACTED> `getState()` from singleton — progress file is persistence artifact, not query source\n- Coordinator's `writeProgressPreservingDetails` calls removed — single writer via subscriber\n\n### Cancel flow\n- Cancel triggered via Health API endpoint only (`POST /cancel` in tools.ts)\n- `transition({ type: 'cancel' })` moves state machine to cancelled state\n- Cooperative cancellation: wave-controller checks `getState().status === 'cancelled'` between substeps\n- In-progress LLM calls finish naturally; no new substeps start\n- Cancelled is a terminal state — explicit reset required (start event implicitly resets from terminal states)\n- Partial results preserved — entities already persisted to KG stay\n\n### Claude's Discretion\n- Exact event type naming and payload shapes\n- How the singleton initializes on module load vs first access\n- Internal structure of the transition function (switch vs map lookup)\n- Error handling in subscribers (catch and log vs propagate)\n- How cooperative cancel check is positioned in the wave-controller loop\n\n</decisions>\n\n<code_context>\n## Existing Code Insights\n\n### Reusable Assets\n- `shared/workflow-types/` (Phase 15): WorkflowState discriminated union, transition types, RunConfig/RunProgress, Zod schemas — the state machine imports and implements these\n- `workflow-events.ts`: CancelWorkflowCommand, StepStatus, WorkflowStartedEvent — some types migrate, others become redundant\n- `workflow-runner.ts`: ProgressUpdate interface, writeProgress functions — replaced by subscriber\n\n### Established Patterns\n- `wave-controller.ts` has `updateProgress()` with ~30 call sites using `{ currentWave, subPhase, message }` shape\n- `coordinator.ts` has `writeProgressPreservingDetails()` — competing writer that must be eliminated\n- `tools.ts` has ad-hoc progress file reads for status <USER_ID_REDACTED> and single-step mode toggles\n- Boolean flags (`singleStepMode`, `mockLLM`, `stepPaused`) scattered in progress file — replaced by RunConfig (immutable) on WorkflowState\n\n### Integration Points\n- `wave-controller.ts`: Primary consumer — all updateProgress calls become transition calls\n- `tools.ts`: Health API — status <USER_ID_REDACTED> switch from file reads to getState(), cancel endpoint added\n- `coordinator.ts`: Remove competing progress writes, may need to import getState() for status checks\n- `workflow-runner.ts`: Progress file write functions replaced by subscriber\n\n</code_context>\n\n<specifics>\n## Specific Ideas\n\n- The singleton pattern with subscribe() naturally sets up Phase 17 (SSE subscriber) and Phase 18 (dashboard) — each phase adds a new subscriber\n- Cooperative cancel with between-substep checks mirrors how the existing single-step pause works (check a flag between steps)\n- The ~8 event types map cleanly to the existing subPhase values in updateProgress, making the migration mechanical\n\n</specifics>\n\n<deferred>\n## Deferred Ideas\n\nNone — discussion stayed within phase scope\n\n</deferred>\n\n---\n\n*Phase: 16-backend-state-machine*\n*Context gathered: 2026-03-10*\n"
